Summary
High-level aggregate views providing at-a-glance metrics and KPIs across your fundraising program.
1 analytics in this category
3.1: Health Checks
 QX39   Monthly Giving Comparison Current vs Prior 2 years Analysis
This report is a vital financial tool that tracks your fundraising revenue pace for the current fiscal year against the
previous two years.
Monthly Giving Comparison Current vs Prior 2 yrs How to use the Monthly Giving Comparison Current vs Prior 2 yrs
analysis This analysis provides a clear, month-by-month comparison of your organization's fundraising performance over
the current and previous two fiscal years, structured according to your fiscal calendar (July-June). It aggregates all gift
amounts by month and fiscal year, allowing you to quickly see trends, seasonal patterns, and the overall direction of giving.
The analysis draws from your Gifts data, using each gift's date and amount, and computes total giving for each month in the
current fiscal year, the prior fiscal year, and two years prior. For each month, it calculates the percentage change in giving
between the current and previous year, flagging instances where new giving has emerged or where there has been a
drop-off. You should use this analysis to understand not only aggregate giving but also identify months where fundraising
has grown, stagnated, or declined, which is invaluable for end-of-year reviews or mid-year course corrections. The primary
metrics-monthly giving totals and year-over-year percentage change-are essential for tracking the health of your donor
pipeline. These figures can alert you to shifts in donor behavior, highlight successful campaigns, or signal the need for
renewed outreach in specific months. By examining these trends, you can better forecast revenue, set realistic targets, and
time your appeals for maximum effectiveness. Development directors and annual giving managers should review this
analysis on a monthly basis. It is handy for identifying which periods require additional engagement or stewardship, and
where to focus personalized outreach. To apply these insights, schedule regular team reviews to discuss months showing
significant change, assign stewardship or solicitation priorities based on emerging trends, and adjust campaign calendars to
align with your strongest periods. Success can be measured by increased year-over-year giving, greater consistency in
monthly revenue, and improved donor retention rates, driven by timely and data-informed engagement. This analysis is
recommended to be reviewed periodically as part of your Constituent Intelligence routines.
Type: Summary | Lifecycle: Portfolio Management | Time: Retrospective | Audience: Strategic
Segments: All/None specified | Scope: Organization

Summary+Detail
Analytics that combine aggregate summaries with drill-down detail, letting you see both the big picture and
individual records.
75 analytics in this category
1.1: Year-over-Year Donation Trends
 QX38   Historical Summary Data Analysis
This analysis (often used as a report) provides a comprehensive, year-over-year historical view of your fundraising
program's core health metrics and KPIs.
Historical Summary Data How to use the Historical Summary Data analysis This analysis provides a year-over-year
summary of your donor activity, helping you track key trends in giving, retention, and donor engagement across fiscal years.
Drawing from your gifts database, it aggregates all gift transactions by constituent (donor), determines each donor's total
giving per fiscal year, and applies a fiscal year definition that aligns with typical nonprofit accounting by rolling the calendar
year forward by six months. The analysis then compiles essential metrics such as the total number of donors, total amount
raised, and, critically, how many donors were retained, newly acquired, or recaptured from lapses. It also calculates the
number of donors lost each year, as well as average and median giving per donor metrics, which provide insight into both
broad trends and shifts in donor generosity. You should use this analysis to monitor donor retention rates, which reveal how
well you are engaging and retaining your supporters over time. The distinction between new, retained, and recaptured
donors allows you to assess the success of both your acquisition and re-engagement strategies. The inclusion of both
average and median giving per donor helps you spot changes in giving patterns-if the average is growing but the median
stays flat, for example, you may be relying on a few large gifts rather than broad-based support. Consider sharing this
output with your annual fund managers and major gift officers to inform their stewardship planning and campaign reviews.
For actionable steps, fundraising directors and development officers should review this analysis at the close of each fiscal
year and midway through the next, as part of their Constituent Intelligence routines. Use the retention and lapsed donor
counts to prioritize which segments need renewed outreach or stewardship. If you notice a decline in new donor acquisition
or average giving, it's a signal to adjust your appeals or donor engagement strategies. Additionally, tracking recaptured
donors can help you refine your strategies for reactivating lapsed donors and evaluate the effectiveness of past campaigns.
To measure the impact of using this analysis, you should track year-over-year improvements in retention rates, total dollars
raised, and the proportion of donors who increase their giving or return after lapsing. Success is reflected in more stable or
growing donor bases and increased giving per donor, which are critical for sustainable fundraising growth.
Type: Summary+Detail | Lifecycle: Acquisition, Retention | Time: Retrospective (Multi-Year) | Audience: Essential
Segments: All/None specified | Scope: Organization
Collections: New Development Director Starter Kit, Board Meeting Prep
Workflows: Annual Fundraising Review (Step 1)
→ Also Try: QX85 Historical YOY Analysis; QX71 Rolling 12 Mo Donor Count and Total Givi

 QX85   Historical Year over Year Analysis
This analysis provides a high-level, year-over-year view of donor retention, acquisition, and overall revenue to assess
overall fundrasing success.
Historical YOY Analysis How to use the Historical YOY Analysis analysis The Historical YOY Analysis gives you a
year-over-year view of donor giving patterns, donor retention, and overall fundraising performance, all built from your actual
giving data. By tracking each donor's total giving by fiscal year and categorizing them into dynamic segments based on
giving thresholds (Top, Middle, and Bottom), you gain actionable insights into how different donor groups contribute to your
mission over time. The analysis draws from the Gifts table, leveraging gift dates and amounts, and uses custom thresholds
stored in your system to define donor tiers. It also identifies key donor lifecycle moments, such as who is retained, who is
new, who has been recaptured after lapsing, and who has lapsed, so you can better understand the flow of your donor
base. You will see annual metrics including the number of donors, total amount raised, median and average gift size, and
the breakdown of giving by donor segment. The analysis calculates retention rates, lapsed donors, and the share of giving
from top, middle, and bottom donors, all of which are essential indicators for evaluating the health and sustainability of your
fundraising program. For instance, the retention rate indicates how well you're keeping donors engaged year after year,
while the recaptured donor metric highlights your success in reactivating lapsed supporters. Strategically, this analysis
empowers you to identify trends—such as shifts in donor retention, growing dependence on top donors, or changes in the
median gift size—that should inform your stewardship and cultivation plans. If you notice a decline in retention or a spike in
lapsed donors, you can target re-engagement campaigns more effectively. The segmentation allows you to tailor
communication and recognition strategies for top, middle, and bottom donors, optimizing your approach for each group.
Scheduling note: This analysis is recommended to be reviewed periodically as part of your Constituent Intelligence routines.
Development directors and donor stewardship teams should review this analysis together, ideally before strategic planning
cycles and after major campaigns. Use the insights to set retention goals, allocate stewardship resources, and personalize
outreach, especially by focusing on recaptured and new donors to build long-term loyalty. Success should be measured by
improvements in donor retention, growth in the number of recaptured donors, and increases in both total and median giving
over time. Regular use of this analysis will help you make data-driven decisions, strengthen constituent relationships, and
drive sustainable growth in fundraising.
Type: Summary+Detail | Lifecycle: Acquisition, Retention | Time: Retrospective (Multi-Year) | Audience: Operational
Segments: All/None specified | Scope: Organization
Collections: New Development Director Starter Kit, Board Meeting Prep, Annual Fund Health Check
Workflows: Annual Fundraising Review (Step 2)
→ Also Try: QX38 Historical Summary Data; QX162 Simple YOY Retention by Segment View; QX139 Multi-Year Revenue Projection;
QX180 Global Revenue Bridge Waterfall -LFY

 QX90   Middle Segment Gift Amount Trends (Annual) Analysis
This analysis (often used as a report) provides a 15-year historical overview of your Middle donor segment across
multiple KPI's.
Middle Segment Gift Amount Trends (Annual) How to use the Middle Segment Gift Amount Trends (Annual) analysis This
analysis provides a year-by-year view of giving patterns specifically among your Middle Segment  donors over the past 15
full fiscal years. It draws from your Gifts data, applying fiscal year logic to align gifts with your organization's reporting
calendar, and cross-references annual donor totals against the thresholds you've defined for what counts as a middle
 donor. By focusing only on years when a constituent s annual giving fell within this middle range, you get a precise
measure of this segment s activity over time. The analysis highlights several key metrics for each fiscal year, including the
number of unique middle donors, the total amount they donated, the average size of each gift, and the median gift amount.
These metrics matter because they reveal both participation and giving trends within this crucial donor group-often the
backbone of sustainable fundraising. For example, you can quickly spot whether the pool of middle donors is growing or
shrinking, whether their giving per gift is increasing, and if the distribution of gifts is shifting (which helps you identify
changes in donor behavior). You should use these insights to inform both annual planning and in-year engagement
strategies. If you see a decline in the number of middle donors, consider targeted stewardship or reactivation campaigns. If
average or median gift sizes are trending upward, you might explore tailored upgrade asks or cultivate major gift prospects
from this segment. This analysis is recommended to be reviewed periodically as part of your Constituent Intelligence
routines to ensure ongoing understanding of donor dynamics. Development directors, annual giving managers, and frontline
fundraisers should all review this analysis together. Use the findings to set segment-specific goals, benchmark current
performance, and identify which donors might benefit from more personalized outreach. If you supplement this analysis with
additional columns—such as donor contact information or engagement history—you can further customize your approach
for each middle donor, enhancing the value of every interaction. Success should be measured by monitoring increases in
retention rates, average gift amounts, and the total giving from the middle segment after you've acted on the insights. You
may also track the number of middle donors who move into higher segments as a result of targeted cultivation. By
leveraging this analysis within your Constituent Intelligence toolkit, you can make smarter decisions and foster stronger
donor relationships.
Type: Summary+Detail | Lifecycle: Portfolio Management | Time: Retrospective (Multi-Year) | Audience: Operational
Segments: Middle | Scope: Segment
Variant Family: Gift Amount Trends (Annual) (segment variants)
→ Also Try: QX93 Middle Segment Gift Size Distribution An
→ Run First: QX172 Segmentation Break Points

 QX91   Bottom Segment Gift Amount Trends (Annual) Analysis
This analysis provides a historical overview of your entry-level donor segment, showing trends across a number of
KPI's.
Bottom Segment Gift Amount Trends (Annual) How to use the Bottom Segment Gift Amount Trends (Annual) analysis This
analysis allows you to understand giving behavior among your lowest annual donor segment, the Bottom Segment, over the
past 15 fiscal years. It leverages your organization's Gifts and Constituent data, specifically focusing on donors whose total
giving in a fiscal year falls below or at a defined bottom_max threshold. By isolating gifts from these donors only during the
years they met the bottom segment criteria, you gain a precise view of the volume, value, and typical size of gifts from this
cohort. You will see, year by year, the number of unique bottom segment donors, the total amount they collectively gave,
and the average and median size of their individual gifts. This segmentation ensures that trends accurately reflect genuine
shifts in engagement among this specific group, rather than being diluted by the contributions of higher-tier donors.  Key
metrics include the number of bottom donors per year, total giving from this group, and both average and median individual
gift amounts. These figures help you monitor the health of your entry-level donor pipeline, identify years of growth or decline,
and spot patterns that may signal opportunities or risks, such as declining participation or shrinking gift sizes. You should
use this analysis to better understand how your acquisition and retention strategies affect lower-tier donors and to inform
tailored stewardship and upgrade efforts. For example, if you observe a downward trend in median gift amount, you might
re-evaluate your messaging or entry-level appeals. If the number of donors in this segment is dropping, it may signal a need
to strengthen acquisition or reactivation campaigns. An annual review by fundraising directors, annual fund managers, and
donor relations staff is recommended, ideally as part of your Constituent Intelligence routines. Apply these insights to
prioritize donor journeys, adjust communication frequency, and test new engagement tactics for this segment. Additionally,
consider segmenting further by donor tenure or channel if you wish to personalize outreach even more. To evaluate the
impact of this analysis, measure changes in bottom segment donor retention, total giving, and the rate at which these
donors are upgraded to higher giving tiers over time. Success will be indicated by increased retention, higher gift totals, and
a healthy pipeline of donors progressing beyond the bottom segment.
Type: Summary+Detail | Lifecycle: Portfolio Management | Time: Retrospective (Multi-Year) | Audience: Operational
Segments: Bottom | Scope: Segment
Variant Family: Gift Amount Trends (Annual) (segment variants)

 QX106   Overall Incremental Lift By Month Analysis
This analysis is a monthly performance dashboard that show which months are contributing above expected to the
current year's fundraising performance.
High Lift Donors LFY AUG How to use the High Lift Donors LFY NOV analysis This analysis identifies donors who have
significantly increased their giving in August of the last full fiscal year compared to their personal average for the same
month across the prior three years. By focusing on this target month and measuring each donor's unique giving lift, you can
pinpoint individuals who are exhibiting strong upward trends—your high lift donors—who may be primed for deeper
engagement or recognition. The analysis uses your Gifts and Constituents data, examining each donor's giving in August
over four years. It calculates the donor's average August giving for the three fiscal years before last year (establishing a
personal baseline), then compares that to their actual giving in August of the previous fiscal year. Only donors whose most
recent August giving exceeded their baseline are included, ensuring you focus on those with genuine, positive momentum.
Key columns include not only the lift calculation, but also each donor s baseline average and actual giving in the latest
August.  These details support a more personalized approach-for example, referencing a donor's consistent loyalty or
recent surge in giving during stewardship or cultivation outreach. The primary metric, Personal Incremental Lift ($),  helps
you move beyond generic segmentation. Rather than just looking at total giving or year-over-year change, you can identify
and prioritize donors whose behavior signals a new level of commitment. This is especially valuable for year-end strategies,
leadership gift prospects, and stewardship planning. You should assign this analysis to development officers for portfolio
review, as well as to annual giving or stewardship teams who are planning touchpoints for the fiscal year. Use the outputs to
trigger timely thank-you calls, targeted upgrade asks, or special recognition for donors whose support is accelerating. For
major gifts officers, these donors may warrant qualification for deeper relationship building. Success can be measured by
tracking subsequent retention and upgrade rates among high-lift donors, as well as by monitoring response rates to
personalized outreach efforts that reference their recent giving lift. This analysis is recommended to be reviewed periodically
as part of your Constituent Intelligence routines, ensuring you consistently capture and respond to emerging donor trends.
Type: Summary+Detail | Lifecycle: Growth/Upgrade | Time: Retrospective | Audience: Operational
Segments: Top, Middle, Bottom | Scope: Segment
Variant Family: Incremental Lift Analysis (dimension variants)
Collections: Annual Fund Health Check
Workflows: Annual Fundraising Review (Step 9)

 QX106   Incremental Lift By Donor Segment Analysis
This analysis provides insight into the incremental lift contribution to your giving total by each segment.
Incremental Lift By Donor Segment How to use the Incremental Lift By Donor Segment analysis This analysis enables you
to see, month by month, how giving from each donor segment-Top, Middle, and Bottom-has changed in the most recent
completed fiscal year compared to the average of the three prior years. It draws on your Gifts data, using constituent IDs,
gift dates, and amounts, as well as your organization's segment thresholds, to categorize donors by annual giving level for
each of the last four fiscal years. By calculating a three-year monthly baseline and comparing it to actual giving in the
previous fiscal year, the analysis reveals the incremental lift (or decline) in giving for each segment and month, expressed
both in dollar value and as a percentage. With this analysis, you gain a clear view into seasonal or campaign-driven shifts in
donor behavior within each segment. The key metric, "Incremental Lift (%)", indicates the percentage change in giving
compared to the historical average, enabling you to identify which segments are outperforming or underperforming
expectations quickly. Understanding these patterns is crucial for making informed decisions, whether you're planning
stewardship, appeals, or reallocating resources for acquisition and retention. Use this analysis to identify periods when
giving surged or lagged, and tailor your engagement accordingly. For example, if "Top" donors gave significantly more in a
particular month, examine what campaigns or communications drove that lift and consider replicating those strategies.
Conversely, if "Middle" or "Bottom" donors dipped below baseline, it may signal a need for re-engagement or a fresh
approach. Reviewing this analysis as part of your Constituent Intelligence routines ensures you stay attuned to real-time
shifts and can act proactively. Fundraising directors, development officers, and campaign managers should review this
analysis on a monthly or quarterly basis. Use the insights to inform segment-specific outreach, adjust annual fund
strategies, and set realistic, data-driven targets for upcoming periods. Success can be measured by tracking increases in
incremental lift percentages over time, improved retention within segments, and more effective allocation of staff and budget
to areas showing the greatest opportunity or need. By integrating these insights into your Constituent Intelligence practices,
you can deepen donor relationships and maximize fundraising outcomes.
Type: Summary+Detail | Lifecycle: Growth/Upgrade | Time: Retrospective | Audience: Operational
Segments: Top, Middle, Bottom | Scope: Segment
Variant Family: Incremental Lift Analysis (dimension variants)
Collections: Annual Fund Health Check
Workflows: Annual Fundraising Review (Step 9)

 QX107   Incremental Lift by New/Existing Analysis
This analysis (often used as a report) provides a detailed performance review between last year and the average over
the prior three years.
Incremental Lift by New/Existing How to use the Incremental Lift by New/Existing analysis This analysis enables you to
measure how giving from new and existing donors in each month of the most recent fiscal year compares to a three-year
historical average, broken out by donor lifecycle stage. It draws on your last four years of gift data, tagging each donation as
either from a "New Donor" (their very first gift) or an "Existing Donor" (any subsequent gift), based on the donor's entire
giving history. For each calendar month, it calculates two key metrics for both groups: the average monthly giving over the
baseline period (the three fiscal years prior to last year) and the actual giving in the most recent full fiscal year. The analysis
then computes the "Incremental Lift (%)", which shows the percentage change in giving compared to the historical average.
You can use this to pinpoint months and donor segments where your fundraising efforts are outperforming or
underperforming the typical pattern, helping you assess the effectiveness of recent campaigns, stewardship, or appeals.
The side-by-side comparison of new versus existing donors allows you to see whether your strategies are driving more
first-time gifts, retaining donors, or increasing gift amounts. The most important calculations to focus on are the "Baseline
Giving (3yr Avg)", "Actual Giving (Last FY)", and "Incremental Lift (%)". These tell you not only whether giving is up or down,
but also highlight seasonal trends and the relative impact of your outreach on different donor groups. Identifying months with
strong positive lift among new donors, for example, can help you replicate successful acquisition tactics. In contrast,
negative trends among existing donors may signal a need for renewed stewardship or re-engagement. You should schedule
this analysis for regular review as part of your Constituent Intelligence routines. Directors of development, annual giving
managers, and donor stewardship teams will benefit most from these insights. Use the findings to tailor your communication
calendar, plan targeted campaigns, and set realistic monthly performance benchmarks for both acquisition and retention.
For example, if you observe a dip in existing donor giving in the first quarter, consider launching a stewardship initiative
during that period. If a new donor giving spikes in a particular month, analyze which campaigns contributed and consider
scaling them. To measure success, track whether your monthly incremental lift improves year-over-year, especially in
priority donor segments. You should also monitor whether adjustments in your outreach lead to stronger retention of new
donors and higher average gifts from existing supporters. By integrating this analysis into your Constituent Intelligence
toolkit, you can make more informed, data-driven decisions that directly support your fundraising goals.
Type: Summary+Detail | Lifecycle: Growth/Upgrade | Time: Retrospective | Audience: Operational
Segments: New | Scope: Organization, Segment
Variant Family: Incremental Lift Analysis (dimension variants)
Collections: Annual Fund Health Check
→ See Summary: QX106 Incremental Lift By Donor Segment

 QX162   Simple YOY Retention by Segment View
This analytic calculates the year-over-year retention rate for each donor segment ('Top', 'Middle', 'Bottom') based on
historical giving data.
This analysis calculates the year-over-year retention rate of donors segmented into 'Top', 'Middle', and 'Bottom' based on
their historical giving data. It leverages thresholds defined in a separate table to classify donors into these segments
according to their total contributions. The data utilized includes donor IDs, gift amounts, and gift dates, allowing for a
comprehensive view of donor behavior over time. Key calculations within this analysis include the determination of how
many unique donors fall into each segment for each fiscal year, as well as the count of those who continue donating in the
subsequent year, specifically within the same segment. This approach allows you to understand retention not only by
segment but also overall, which is crucial for identifying trends in donor loyalty. The insights derived from this analysis are
invaluable for strategic decision-making. By knowing the retention rates across different donor segments, you can identify
which groups are most engaged and which may need additional outreach or support. For instance, if the retention rate for
'Top' donors is significantly higher than that of 'Bottom' donors, you might focus your efforts on enhancing the engagement
strategies for the lower segment to boost their loyalty. You should consider running this analysis at the end of each fiscal
year, as it will provide a clear picture of how effective your donor engagement strategies have been over the past year.
Development officers and fundraising directors should review the findings to adjust strategies accordingly. For instance, if
you notice a decline in retention within a particular segment, it may be an opportunity to implement targeted campaigns to
re-engage those donors. To measure the success of applying insights from this analysis, you can track changes in retention
rates over time after implementing new strategies. Additionally, monitoring the overall increase in total donations from each
segment can provide a direct measure of the impact your adjusted engagement efforts are having. Evaluating donor
feedback after specific outreach initiatives can also give qualitative insights into whether your strategies resonate with
donors, further refining your approach.
Type: Summary+Detail | Lifecycle: Retention | Time: Retrospective (Multi-Year) | Audience: Essential
Segments: Top, Middle, Bottom | Scope: Segment
Collections: New Development Director Starter Kit, Board Meeting Prep, Annual Fund Health Check
Workflows: Quarterly Strategic Review (Step 4), Annual Fundraising Review (Step 5)

1.2: Revenue Concentration Analysis
 QX83   Top 50 Gifts Last Fiscal Year Analysis
This analysis (often used as a report) reveals the organization's reliance on its most generous supporters.
Top 50 Gifts Last FY How to use the Top 50 Gifts Last FY analysis This analysis identifies the 50 largest gifts received by
your organization in the last full fiscal year. Use this as another way to quickly see how much of your annual fundraising
relies on your largest donors, and how concentrated your fundraising base is, as well as how much of your overall giving
revenue comes from this segment of large gifts.  .These numbers matter because they reveal your organization's
fundraising dependency on a select group and highlight opportunities or risks if those donors change their behavior.
Strategically, you should review this last fiscal year analysis annually as part of your Constituent Intelligence routines.
Development directors, major gifts officers, and stewardship teams should utilize these insights to prioritize
relationship-building efforts, establish realistic fundraising targets, and design personalized engagement plans for their top
donors from this list.
Type: Summary+Detail | Lifecycle: Portfolio Management | Time: Retrospective (LFY) | Audience: Operational
Segments: All/None specified | Scope: Organization
Collections: Major Gift Officer Daily Driver

 QX145   Historical Individual vs Organizational
Historical analysis of the annual giving split between individual donors and organizational donors.
This analysis provides a comprehensive view of the annual giving landscape by comparing contributions from individual
donors versus organizational donors. It utilizes data on gifts made over multiple fiscal years, classifying each donor based
on whether they are an individual or part of an organization. The analysis calculates total giving amounts, the number of
donors in each category, and identifies top-tier individual donors based on a specified minimum giving threshold. The key
calculations include the total annual giving for individuals and organizations, the number of unique donors in each category,
and median contributions for both top individuals and organizations. Understanding these metrics is essential as they reveal
not only the overall financial contributions but also highlight the engagement levels of different donor segments. For
instance, tracking the number of top segment individuals can help you identify your most valuable supporters, while
assessing organizational giving can provide insights into how well you are engaging with corporate partners. Strategically,
this analysis equips you with critical insights to refine fundraising strategies and enhance donor relationships. By
understanding the trends in individual versus organizational giving, you can tailor your outreach efforts. For example, if
individual giving is declining, you might consider strategies to re-engage those donors through personalized communication
or targeted campaigns. Conversely, if organizational giving is strong, you may want to explore ways to deepen these
partnerships or leverage them for matching gift opportunities. You should consider running this analysis annually, ideally at
the close of the fiscal year, to align with your reporting and strategy planning cycles. Development officers, fundraising
directors, and donor relations teams should review the findings to inform their strategies. The insights can guide decisions
on where to allocate resources for donor engagement efforts, helping you to strengthen relationships with both individual
and organizational supporters. To measure the success of using this analysis, track changes in donor retention rates, the
growth of contributions from both segments over time, and the effectiveness of targeted campaigns based on the insights
gained. You could also evaluate the impact of specific initiatives aimed at increasing engagement with top-tier individual
donors or enhancing connections with organizational partners, looking for measurable increases in giving or participation in
fundraising events. By leveraging the insights from this analysis, you can drive more effective fundraising strategies and
foster stronger, more meaningful connections with your donor base.

 QX41   Giving Pyramid Analysis Last Fiscal Year
This analysis breaks down your fundraising results from the last full fiscal year into a "giving pyramid," showing sizes
and counts of gifts by size level.
Giving Pyramid Analysis LFY How to use the Giving Pyramid Analysis LFY analysis This analysis transforms your last full
fiscal year's gift data into a clear giving pyramid, allowing you to visualize the distribution of donors and gifts across different
giving levels. By categorizing each gift from the Gifts table by amount into familiar ranges (for example, $0-$ 99.99, $100-$
499.99, up to $100,000+), you gain immediate insight into how your donor base is structured, from grassroots supporters to
major donors. The analysis draws on every gift made during the last complete fiscal year, automatically adjusting for your
fiscal calendar, and summarizes several key metrics for each giving level: the number of gifts, the number of unique donors,
the total dollars contributed, as well as the average, median, smallest, and largest gift sizes. This set of analyses is
compelling for fundraising strategy because it not only shows where your revenue is concentrated, but also highlights areas
for growth and improvement. The calculation of the percentage of total giving by level clarifies which donor segments drive
your fundraising results and which are underrepresented. Metrics like median and average gift size help you understand
typical giving behavior at each level, revealing opportunities for targeted stewardship or upgrades. You should use these
insights to identify gaps in your pyramid, such as a thin mid-level or an overreliance on a handful of major donors, and
design tailored cultivation and solicitation strategies. Fundraising directors and development officers should review this
analysis together as part of regular Constituent Intelligence routines-ideally quarterly or after major campaigns. Use it to
prioritize your portfolio management: for instance, assign stewardship actions to retain top-tier donors, or identify prospects
for mid-level upgrades. Additionally, you can focus outreach on expanding the base at entry-level tiers, or mobilize board
members to help fill gaps in the pyramid. Success can be measured by tracking year-over-year improvements in donor
retention and upgrades within each level, as well as by the diversification of gift sources and increased stability in overall
revenue. By integrating these insights into your strategic planning, you'll strengthen donor relationships and build a more
resilient fundraising program.

 QX92   Top Segment Gift Size Distribution Analysis (Annual)
This analysis provides a 15-year historical overview of your top donor segment, breaking down the distribution of
individual gift sizes by percentile.
Top Segment Gift Size Distribution Analysis (Annual) How to use the Top Segment Gift Size Distribution Analysis (Annual)
analysis This analysis provides a detailed, year-by-year view of giving patterns among your top donors over the past 15
completed fiscal years, utilizing your organization's Gift, Thresholds, and Constituent data. It calculates, for each fiscal year,
which donors reached or surpassed your defined top annual giving threshold and then examines the full range of their gifts
for that year.  You can use this to see not only how many donors qualified as Top each year, but also the exact distribution
of gift sizes within that segment, including the total given by the group, the 25th, 50th (median), and 75th percentile gift
values, and the single largest gift. These metrics enable you to identify shifts in giving patterns, such as whether your top
donors are becoming increasingly concentrated among a few very large gifts or whether the group is broadening, and to
measure the impact of stewardship efforts or major campaigns. You should review this analysis at least annually-ideally as
part of your Constituent Intelligence routines-but consider more frequent reviews if you are planning a campaign or
reassessing major gift strategies. Development directors, prospect managers, and annual fund leaders should use the
insights to tailor stewardship and solicitation strategies  and identify opportunities for personal outreach. For instance, a
sudden jump in the 75th percentile gift might signal a few donors increasing their support, warranting personalized
recognition or cultivation. If the number of top donors is declining, you should investigate retention and engagement tactics.
Apply the findings by adjusting your stewardship plans for top donors, targeting those who are near the threshold for
upgrade opportunities, and ensuring that your segmentation accurately reflects current donor behavior. Measure success by
tracking increases in top-segment retention, total dollars raised from this group, and movement of donors into higher giving
brackets year over year. This analysis empowers you to deploy resources more effectively and strengthen your most
valuable donor relationships.

 QX93   Middle Segment Gift Size Distribution Analysis (Annual)
This analysis (often used as a report) provides a 15-year historical overview of the sizes of gifts from your mid-level
donor segment.
Middle Segment Gift Size Distribution Analysis (Annual) How to use the Middle Segment Gift Size Distribution Analysis
(Annual) analysis This analysis helps you understand long-term giving patterns among your Middle donor segment over the
past fifteen fiscal years. It draws on your gifts and constituent records, focusing on annual giving totals for each donor and
identifying those who fall within your organization's defined Middle giving thresholds for any given year. Once Middle donors
are identified for each year, they are examined for all gifts they made during their qualifying years, while ensuring that only
living donors are included. You gain year-over-year insights into how many donors qualified for the Middle segment, how
much they collectively contributed, and the distribution of individual gift amounts within the segment. Key metrics calculated
in this analysis include the number of Middle donors per year, total giving from this segment, and important gift size
percentiles-the 25th, 50th (median), and 75th percentiles-along with the largest gift made in each year. These percentile
figures help you understand the typical and outlier gift sizes, allowing you to set appropriate ask amounts, stewardship
strategies, and campaign targets. By tracking these metrics annually, you can spot trends, such as segment growth,
contraction, or changes in giving behaviors, that inform your fundraising planning. Strategically, you should use these
insights to refine your engagement tactics with Middle donors. For example, if you see that the median gift is rising, you
might adjust your suggested gift amounts or stewardship tiers accordingly. If you notice donor counts declining, you may
want to prioritize retention efforts or develop targeted upgrade strategies. This analysis is particularly useful for annual
giving managers, major gifts officers, and any team members responsible for donor segmentation and mid-level donor
programs. Development leadership should review the analysis when setting budget projections or prioritizing
relationship-building efforts. You can apply these insights to personalize outreach, set more accurate fundraising goals for
the Middle segment, and identify opportunities for donor upgrades. You may want to supplement the analysis with additional
donor-level details, such as engagement history or communication preferences. In that case, you'll be even better equipped
to tailor your stewardship and maximize donor lifetime value. Schedule this analysis to be reviewed periodically as part of
your Constituent Intelligence routines. To evaluate its impact, track metrics such as year-over-year retention in the Middle
segment, changes in average and median gift size, and the number of donors successfully upgraded to higher segments.
Consistent use will help you make more informed, data-driven decisions that drive sustained fundraising growth.

 QX179   Giving Pyramid Detail -Donor View
This analytic provides a donor centric view of the gifts that make up the Giving Pyramid.
The Giving Pyramid Detail - Donor View analysis provides a comprehensive examination of individual donor gifts within the
current fiscal year. The analysis focuses on categorizing donor contributions into various tiers based on the gift amount,
allowing you to understand the distribution of donations across different levels. It utilizes data from the Gifts table,
concentrating exclusively on donations made in the current fiscal year, which is calculated by adding six months to the
current date to align with many fiscal year reporting standards. The analysis breaks down donor gifts into six monetary
categories: less than $100, between $100 and $499.99, between $500 and $2,499.99, between $2,500 and $9,999.99,
between $10,000 and $99,999.99, and $100,000 and above. For each donor, it calculates the count and total amount of
gifts in each category, providing a clear view of their contribution patterns. Additionally, it summarizes the total number of
gifts and the total giving amount for each donor throughout the year. These metrics are crucial as they help pinpoint where
most donations are concentrated, identify major donors, and recognize potential growth areas within your donor base. By
examining these tiers, you can tailor your engagement strategies, such as personalized communications or targeted
campaigns, to different donor segments, thereby enhancing the effectiveness of your fundraising efforts. To maximize the
strategic value of this analysis, consider running it at the end of each quarter to track changes and trends in donor behavior
over time. Development officers and fundraising directors should review the findings to identify both high-value donors and
those who might be encouraged to increase their giving. The insights can also guide the planning of donor recognition
programs or the allocation of resources to cultivate relationships with donors poised to move into higher giving tiers.
Success measures for this analysis could include an increase in donor retention rates, growth in average donation size, and
a higher number of donors transitioning to upper giving tiers. By assessing these outcomes, you can gauge the
effectiveness of strategies informed by this analysis and make data-driven decisions to optimize your fundraising initiatives.

 QX7   Giving Tuesday Only Donors Analysis
This analysis isolates a transactional group of donors who only give on Giving Tuesday, highlighting an opportunity to
build a deeper relationship.
Giving Tuesday Only Donors How to use the Giving Tuesday Only Donors analysis This analysis identifies donors who have
given exclusively on Giving Tuesday over the past five fiscal years. Drawing on your gift transaction history, it focuses on
individuals whose only recorded gifts during this period were made specifically on the recognized Giving Tuesday dates.
The analysis leverages gift dates, donor identifiers, and supporting details, such as whether the donor is flagged as an
organization or an individual, helping you pinpoint a unique donor segment with highly concentrated giving behavior. By
calculating both the total number of gifts per donor and the proportion of those gifts that fall on Giving Tuesday, this analysis
highlights constituents whose engagement is entirely tied to this single annual campaign. This specificity matters because it
surfaces individuals who may be responsive only to highly visible, time-bound appeals, and who have not participated in
your fundraising efforts at other times. You can use these findings to refine your stewardship and campaign planning, as
these donors present both a retention opportunity and a challenge to deepen their involvement. In addition to core metrics,
the analysis includes columns such as each donor s name and whether they are an individual or organizational donor.
These supporting details enable you to craft more personalized follow-up strategies, tailoring outreach to donor type and
past communication preferences. With this intelligence, your team can segment communications, recognize Giving Tuesday
loyalty, and experiment with targeted asks outside of the Giving Tuesday window. You should have major gift officers,
annual fund managers, and digital fundraising leads review this analysis as part of your Constituent Intelligence routines,
ideally in the weeks following Giving Tuesday and ahead of yearly planning. First, consider sending personalized
thank-yous that reference their Giving Tuesday support. Second, develop a re-engagement sequence to invite these donors
to participate in other campaigns or events throughout the year. Third, analyze whether specific demographics or
organizational connections are overrepresented in this group, informing your acquisition and stewardship strategies. To
measure success, track year-over-year retention of these donors, monitor conversion rates as you invite them to participate
outside Giving Tuesday, and assess any lift in overall giving amounts attributable to targeted outreach. By integrating this
analysis into your regular review cycle, you can drive smarter engagement and better donor outcomes.

Monthly Fundraising Baseline How to use the Monthly Fundraising Baseline analysis This analysis establishes your

up-to-date and seasonally sensitive baseline that reflects real donor behavior. The data is drawn directly from your gift and
constituent records, identifying every donor's fiscal year engagement and then categorizing their status as New, Retained,
or Recaptured for each year. This segmentation allows you to see not only overall monthly trends but also how different
donor cohorts contribute to your fundraising outcomes throughout the year. Key metrics produced include the average total
giving per month, the average number of unique donors per month, and the average giving amounts segmented by donor
status: Retained, New, and Recaptured. Understanding these patterns is vital: for example, a spike in giving from New
donors in December might indicate successful acquisition campaigns, whereas consistent giving from Retained donors in
May could reflect the strength of your stewardship efforts. By comparing current performance against these baselines, you
can quickly identify when a month is underperforming or exceeding expectations, and which donor group is driving those
changes. You should use this analysis to inform campaign planning, budgeting, and donor communications strategy.
Development directors and annual giving managers will find it particularly useful for setting realistic monthly targets, timing
appeals to coincide with seasonal giving peaks, and assessing the impact of new initiatives. For example, if you notice a dip
in Retained donor giving during the summer months, you might schedule targeted stewardship touchpoints in late spring.

are most responsive in each period. This analysis is recommended to be reviewed periodically as part of your Constituent
Intelligence routines. Review it before launching major campaigns, during quarterly fundraising reviews, and when
forecasting revenue to ensure accuracy. Success should be measured by improved accuracy in monthly revenue
projections, increased retention or reactivation of lapsed donors, and the ability to proactively address unexpected dips in
giving. By embedding these insights into your workflow, you ll strengthen donor relationships and maximize fundraising
effectiveness throughout the year.

 QX136   Annual Tier Transition Stats- Basic Analysis
This is a high-level, strategic analysis (often used as a report) that measures the health and fluidity of your donor
pipeline.
Annual Tier Transition Stats- Basic How to use the Annual Tier Transition Stats- Basic analysis This analysis provides a
clear, year-over-year view of how your donors transition between giving tiers —  Top, Middle, and Bottom—based on their
annual giving totals. By examining your Gifts data and classifying each donor by segment for every fiscal year, it then tracks
whether each donor upgrades, downgrades, maintains their segment, or lapses the following year. The thresholds that
define each segment are drawn from your organization's own standards, ensuring that the segmentation aligns with your
unique fundraising model. At its core, this analysis calculates the percentage of donors in each tier who take each possible
transition path: upgrading to a higher tier, maintaining their current position, dropping to a lower tier, or lapsing (not giving at
all the following year). These transition rates are essential for understanding not just retention, but the health and
momentum of your donor pipeline. By filtering out deceased constituents and excluding the most recent fiscal year (since
transitions can't be measured for donors who have not yet had a next year), it focuses on actionable, up-to-date insights.
You can use these findings to strengthen your Constituent Intelligence efforts. For example, seeing a high upgrade
percentage among Bottom-tier donors might prompt you to invest in targeted cultivation or stewardship for that group. If you
notice that middle-tier donors have a high lapse or downgrade rate, it signals a need to reinforce engagement before
attrition sets in. The analysis also helps you identify which segments are most stable, letting you allocate resources for
maximum impact. Fundraising directors and development officers should review this analysis at least annually, ideally as
part of regular Constituent Intelligence routines. Major gift officers can use the insights to prioritize outreach to donors likely
to upgrade, while stewardship teams can design interventions for those at risk of lapsing or downgrading. Consider sharing
results with your board or leadership to highlight progress and inform strategy. Success should be measured by tracking
improvements in upgrade and maintenance rates, reductions in lapses, and ultimately, growth in total giving from each
segment over time. If you use this analysis to guide targeted interventions and then see positive movement in these metrics,
you can be confident your Constituent Intelligence approach is driving stronger donor relationships and program outcomes.

Annual Tier Transition Analysis-By Tier How to use the Annual Tier Transition Analysis-By Tier analysis This analysis

their annual giving totals. By examining every donor's giving history, it assigns each donor to a segment for every fiscal

their total four-year giving impact and lifetime value.
This analysis identifies individual donors who have maintained a consecutive giving streak over three years and evaluates
their retention status in the fourth year. By categorizing these donors based on their giving segment in the third year, you
gain valuable insights into donor loyalty and engagement. The analysis draws on data from your Gifts and Constituents
tables, focusing on gift amounts, donor identities, and segments defined by established thresholds. The aim is to assess
whether these donors continued their support into the fourth year, thus providing clarity on donor retention. Key metrics
include the total giving amount in the fourth year, the total giving over the four-year span, and the cumulative lifetime giving
for each donor. The categorization of donors into segments-Top, Middle, or Bottom-based on their giving amounts helps you
understand patterns in donor behavior and loyalty. The retention classification, denoted as "Retained" or "Lapsed," offers
actionable insights into which donor segments are engaging effectively with your organization and which may require
additional attention or strategies to improve retention. Utilizing this analysis allows you to make informed decisions
regarding fundraising strategies and donor engagement. By assessing donor loyalty, you can tailor your communication and

This understanding of donor behavior helps you allocate your resources more effectively, ensuring that you focus on

the most recent data on donor retention. It is particularly useful for fundraising directors and development officers who are

high-value donors or revitalizing relationships with those who have lapsed. To measure the success of implementing this

 QX170   3-Year Consecutive Donor Value -Needs Work Analysis

3-Year Consecutive Donor Value -Needs Work How to use the 3-Year Consecutive Donor Value -Needs Work analysis This
analysis identifies donors who have given for three consecutive fiscal years prior to the most recently completed fiscal year,
allowing you to understand patterns of consistent giving and predict future retention potential. Drawing on your Gifts and

upgrades or declines. This analysis is most valuable when reviewed by your fundraising directors, annual giving teams, and
major gifts officers as part of your Constituent Intelligence routines. Use it to identify loyal donors with high upgrade
potential, flag those at risk of lapsing, and refine your segmentation for appeals or stewardship campaigns. For example, if
you see strong retention but stagnant giving in a segment, you might introduce tailored upgrade asks; if retention drops
among mid-level donors, consider enhanced recognition or personal outreach. Assign responsibility for reviewing these
trends and following up with targeted strategies for each cohort. To measure success, track changes in retention rates,
average annual giving, and the proportion of donors advancing to higher giving tiers over time. You should see improved
retention and increased giving in your most engaged segments if you use these insights to focus your efforts and
personalize your approach.

 QX22   Upgrade/Downgrade Patterns All Donors Analysis
This report provides a historical analysis of how your most valuable donors move between giving tiers from one year
to the next.
Upgrade/Downgrade Patterns All Donors How to use the Upgrade/Downgrade Patterns All Donors -Review Later analysis
This analysis tracks year-over-year giving patterns for all donors, specifically focusing on whether each donor has
upgraded, downgraded, or maintained their annual giving between fiscal years. It uses your historical giving data, grouping
each donor's gifts by fiscal year (adjusted for a July-June fiscal year), and then segments donors into "Top" or "Middle" tiers
based on annual giving thresholds you define in your Thresholds table. The analysis then compares each donor's giving tier
from one year to the next, labeling their transition as an upgrade (moving from Middle to Top), downgrade (from Top to
Middle), or maintained (staying in the same tier). You will see, for each fiscal year pair and giving tier, the number of donors
who upgraded, downgraded, or maintained their tier, along with average and median gift totals for each group. The
percentage calculation helps you quickly assess the proportion of each transition type within a tier, making it easy to spot
trends such as retention among top donors or opportunities for middle-tier donors to move up. These metrics are central to
Constituent Intelligence, allowing you to measure the effectiveness of your stewardship and upgrade strategies over time.
Use this analysis to identify patterns in donor mobility and inform targeted engagement efforts. For example, if you see a
high rate of downgrades among top-tier donors, it may prompt a review of your stewardship practices. Conversely, a healthy
rate of upgrades from middle to top tier signals effective engagement or campaign strategies that could be replicated.
Fundraising directors, annual giving managers, and anyone responsible for donor retention and growth should review this
regularly to inform both mass and personalized outreach efforts. Scheduling note: This analysis is recommended to be
reviewed periodically as part of your Constituent Intelligence routines. To apply these insights, you can prioritize personal
outreach to donors who have recently downgraded, as they may be at risk of further attrition, and celebrate or further
engage those who have upgraded as potential major gift prospects. Success can be measured by tracking increases in
upgrade rates, decreases in downgrades, and overall improvement in donor retention within each giving tier across review
cycles. Consistently leveraging this analysis will help you fine-tune your donor journey strategies and ultimately drive
stronger fundraising outcomes.

 QX8   Top Level Donor Loyalty Analysis
This analysis analyzes the long-term loyalty of your major donors, focusing on the consistency of their top-tier support
over many years.
Top Level Donor Loyalty Analysis How to use the Active Top Level Donor Loyalty Analysis analysis This analysis identifies
and profiles your most loyal top-level donors, focusing on those whose annual giving has consistently met or exceeded your
organization's "top donor" threshold. Using data from constituent records and gift histories, the analysis calculates several
key loyalty metrics, including the total number of years a donor has given at the top tier, their longest streak of consecutive
top-tier years, and whether they are currently maintaining such a streak. It also highlights each donor's total lifetime giving
and the most recent year in which they contributed, providing a comprehensive picture of their engagement trajectory. You
will find that the analysis not only surfaces the core loyalty calculations but also provides supporting information, such as
donor names, whether the donor is an organization, and their deceased status. These additional columns are essential for
personalizing your stewardship and tailoring outreach, allowing your team to recognize organizational donors differently and
to avoid outreach to deceased individuals. The primary metrics — current consecutive streak, maximum consecutive years,
total years at top level, and most recent gift year—clarify which donors are sustaining or increasing their high-level support,
and which may be at risk of lapsing. For instance, a declining current streak or an absence of a recent gift may indicate a
need for immediate engagement. Conversely, a long consecutive streak highlights donors worthy of special recognition or
cultivation for legacy giving. Strategically, you can utilize these insights to prioritize relationship-building with your most loyal
supporters, to intervene proactively with donors whose top-level giving streaks may be coming to an end, and to segment
your stewardship efforts by loyalty patterns rather than just by "giving amount". Fundraising directors and frontline gift
officers should review this analysis regularly, ideally in portfolio review meetings, to spot opportunities for personalized
touches, targeted asks, or timely re-engagement. This analysis is recommended to be reviewed periodically as part of your
Constituent Intelligence routines. To evaluate the effectiveness of this analysis, track subsequent donor retention rates
among top-tier donors, the reactivation of lapsed streaks, and the growth in multi-year high-level giving. Success will be
reflected in improved donor retention, increased development of the major gift pipeline, and more meaningful, data-driven
stewardship actions.

Constituents data and referencing your segmentation thresholds, the analysis spotlights first-time donors at higher giving

donor type (individual or organization), the giving segment they qualify for, and the number of months since their first and
only donation. These supporting columns are valuable for tailoring your outreach, as they provide context for timing,
potential gift capacity, and donor profile. The key metric here is identifying those who made a significant initial gift but have
not returned, filtered by your organization's own definitions of middle and top donors, ensuring you focus on constituents
with the most strategic value. The Months Since Gift calculation pinpoints donors who are within a critical window where a
personalized intervention is most likely to be effective, while segmenting by giving level helps you prioritize your stewardship
efforts. Strategically, this analysis enables you to target high-potential donors before they fully lapse, supporting more
effective re-engagement campaigns and personalized stewardship. Development directors and major gifts officers should
review this analysis regularly-ideally as part of your Constituent Intelligence routines-to coordinate timely follow-up and craft
messaging that acknowledges the donor s prior impact and invites renewed involvement. For actionable next steps, assign
relationship managers or stewardship staff to personally review these donors and develop individualized outreach
strategies, such as tailored thank-you calls, invitations to special events, or impact updates referencing their specific gift.

these donors, measure changes in retention for middle and top first-time givers, and monitor the total revenue recovered
from this group over time. These success measures will help demonstrate the value added by targeted Constituent
Intelligence and guide ongoing improvements in your donor engagement strategy.

stewardship plans, knowing not just who gave, but exactly when and how much. It lets you reference recent activity and

donors in each fiscal year. This percentile threshold is important because it highlights donors whose giving behavior is
notably stronger than their peers, suggesting they may be receptive to more ambitious asks or deeper engagement. By
focusing on these donors, you can prioritize your efforts where the potential for an upgrade is highest. Strategically, you
should use this analysis to inform mid-level donor pipeline development and early-stage major gift qualification. It is

conversion rates from bottom to middle or higher segments, and overall revenue lift from this cohort. Over time, you should
see improved donor retention, higher average gifts, and a more robust mid-level pipeline.

 QX108   High Lift Donors DEC Last Fiscal Year Analysis
This analysis provides a retrospective look at the donors whose contribitions provided the greatest uplift to December
fundraising results last year.
High Lift Donors DEC LFY How to use the High Lift Donors DEC LFY analysis This analysis identifies donors who made
gifts in December of the last full fiscal year that exceeded their own average December giving over the previous three years.
Using your giving data, it compares each donor's most recent December performance to their typical December support,
highlighting those individuals whose giving has meaningfully increased-these are your high-lift donors. The analysis draws
on all gift records, calculates three-year baselines for each donor, and isolates those who surpassed their own historical
benchmarks in December. It surfaces not only the incremental dollar lift but also supporting details such as the donor's
name and constituent ID, which allows you to personalize your outreach quickly. The core metric, Personal Incremental Lift
($),  measures the difference between a donor's actual December giving in the last fiscal year and their own three-year
average for December. This approach highlights genuine accelerations in donor engagement, rather than focusing solely on
large gifts or single-year performance. By filtering for donors who are not marked as deceased and who gave more than
their average, you ensure the analysis focuses on living donors, showing positive movement. You can use this analysis to
guide strategic stewardship and cultivation efforts. For example, prioritize high-lift donors for thank-you calls, personal
notes, or invitations to special events, as their increased support signals a deepening commitment. The inclusion of donor
names and IDs facilitates tailored outreach, as development officers can reference specific giving patterns or acknowledge
year-over-year growth in communications, thereby strengthening the donor relationship. Reviewing this analysis regularly,
especially as part of your Constituent Intelligence routines, ensures you don't miss emerging major gift prospects or
significant shifts in donor loyalty. Fundraising directors and gift officers should review this analysis shortly after each
December close and before major stewardship pushes. Use the insights to segment high lift donors for personalized
recognition or to identify candidates for upgrade strategies and leadership giving programs. Success can be measured by
tracking follow-up actions taken for these donors, as well as subsequent retention and upgrade rates, and the overall growth
in the high-lift cohort year over year. By focusing on these metrics, you can effectively leverage Constituent Intelligence to
drive increased giving and deepen donor engagement.

month across the prior three years. By focusing on this target month and measuring each donor's unique giving lift, you can
pinpoint individuals who are exhibiting strong upward trends—your high lift donors—who may be primed for deeper
engagement or recognition. The analysis uses your Gifts and Constituents data, examining each donor's giving in
November over four years. It calculates the donor's average November giving for the three fiscal years before last year
(establishing a personal baseline), then compares that to their actual giving in November of the previous fiscal year. Only
donors whose most recent November giving exceeded their baseline are included, ensuring you focus on those with
genuine, positive momentum. Key columns include not only the lift calculation, but also each donor s baseline average and
actual giving in the latest November.  These details support a more personalized approach-for example, referencing a
donor's consistent loyalty or recent surge in giving during stewardship or cultivation outreach. The primary metric, Personal
Incremental Lift ($),  helps you move beyond generic segmentation. Rather than just looking at total giving or year-over-year
change, you can identify and prioritize donors whose behavior signals a new level of commitment. This is especially
valuable for year-end strategies, leadership gift prospects, and stewardship planning. You should assign this analysis to
development officers for portfolio review, as well as to annual giving or stewardship teams who are planning touchpoints for
the fiscal year. Use the outputs to trigger timely thank-you calls, targeted upgrade asks, or special recognition for donors
whose support is accelerating. For major gifts officers, these donors may warrant qualification for deeper relationship
building. Success can be measured by tracking subsequent retention and upgrade rates among high-lift donors, as well as
by monitoring response rates to personalized outreach efforts that reference their recent giving lift. This analysis is
recommended to be reviewed periodically as part of your Constituent Intelligence routines, ensuring you consistently
capture and respond to emerging donor trends.

 QX17   Segment Graduation Rates Analysis
This analysis (often used as a report) tracks donor movement between giving segments, measures graduation rates,
retention, and lapse patterns.
Segment Graduation Rates How to use the Segment Graduation Rates analysis This analysis provides a clear,
year-over-year view of how your donors transition between giving segments—Top, Middle, and Bottom—based on their total
annual giving, using your organization's own customizable thresholds. By examining the gift history of each constituent over
the past six fiscal years (adjusted to your fiscal calendar), it identifies whether a donor has upgraded to a higher segment,
maintained their giving level, downgraded, or lapsed entirely in the following year. The analysis draws on your Gifts and
Constituents data,  focusing on recent, relevant giving histories. You gain actionable insights into donor migration patterns,
revealing which segments are most stable, where upgrades or downgrades are most likely to occur, and which segments
face the greatest risk of attrition. The analysis summarizes these transitions with clear metrics: total number of donors in
each starting segment, and the rates of upgrade, retention, downgrade, and lapse. These rates are particularly valuable for
targeting stewardship efforts and evaluating the effectiveness of your donor engagement strategies. For example, a high
lapse rate among Middle donors may signal the need for more personalized outreach, while a strong upgrade rate in Bottom
 donors could help you refine your annual fund appeals or mid-level pipeline cultivation. This analysis is recommended to be
reviewed periodically as part of your Constituent Intelligence routines, especially by fundraising directors, development
officers, and anyone responsible for donor stewardship or segmentation strategy. You should use these insights to prioritize
outreach to donors at risk of downgrading or lapsing, tailor your communications to celebrate upgrades and maintainers,
and evaluate the impact of specific stewardship or solicitation initiatives on segment movement.  To measure success, track
improvements in upgrade and retention rates within each segment over time, reductions in lapse rates, and the movement
of donors into higher-value segments. Ultimately, incorporating this analysis into your Constituent Intelligence process will
help you focus resources where they can have the greatest impact and build a stronger, more loyal donor base.

 QX25   Middle to Top Donor Pathway Analysis
This analysis analyzes the long-term effectiveness of your mid-level program as a pipeline for producing future major
donors.
Middle to Top Donor Pathway How to use the Middle to Top Donor Pathway analysis This analysis helps you understand
how your middle-tier donors progress to become top donors over time, providing actionable insights into your donor pipeline
and upgrade strategies. It draws on your historic gift data, classifying each donor's annual giving by fiscal year and
segmenting them into Basic, Middle,   or Top  tiers based on thresholds you define in your Thresholds table. By tracking
how long it takes for a middle donor to become a top donor, along with the frequency and amount of their giving, you gain a
clear picture of upgrade pathways within your constituent base. You will see core metrics, including the total number of
middle-tier donors upgraded in each fiscal year, the overall pool of middle-tier donors, and the percentage of middle-tier
donors who upgraded. The analysis also highlights the average years it takes for an upgrade, giving you insight into the
typical donor journey. Additional metrics, such as average starting and upgrade amounts, average giving frequency, and the
proportion of frequent givers who upgrade, help identify characteristics associated with successful transitions. For instance,
knowing how many donors upgrade within the very next year or within three years allows you to tailor engagement timing
and stewardship efforts more precisely. This analysis is particularly valuable for development officers and directors
responsible for growing major gift pipelines and enhancing donor retention. By reviewing this as part of your regular
Constituent Intelligence routines, you can identify which years or donor segments are most responsive to upgrade
strategies, and where additional cultivation might yield the highest returns. Fundraisers should examine the characteristics
of those who have moved up quickly or given frequently, and use that information to prioritize outreach, personalize
stewardship messages, and design targeted campaigns. Major gift officers should use the insights to select middle donors
for proactive cultivation, focusing on those who resemble past successful upgrades. To measure success, track the
increase in upgrade percentages over time, the reduction in average years to upgrade, and the growth in average upgrade
amounts. You should also monitor the responsiveness of frequent givers to tailored outreach, as indicated by the Pct
Frequent Givers ■ measure. Ultimately, use this analysis to inform your moves management processes and to drive
strategic, data-informed decisions that strengthen your donor pipeline and deepen relationships.

 QX68   All Donor Recaptures (10yr) - most recent recapture event only Analysis
This analysis identifies the donors who, after lapsing for more than a year, made a comeback gift within the last 10
fiscal years.
All Donor Recaptures (10yr) - most recent recapture event only How to use the All Donor Recaptures (10yr) - most recent
recapture event only analysis This analysis identifies every donor your organization has successfully recaptured in the last
ten fiscal years, focusing on their most recent instance of returning after a lapse of at least one year without giving. It draws
from your constituent, gift, and segmentation data to surface patterns in donor lapses and recoveries, highlighting each
donor's giving level before they lapsed, their giving level at the moment of recapture, the duration of their inactivity, and their
most recent fiscal year status. By leveraging Constituent Intelligence, you gain precise visibility into which lapsed donors
have been re-engaged, enabling you to understand their giving journeys better. You will see each donor s name, the fiscal
years relevant to their lapse and recapture, their giving totals and segment (Top, Middle, or Bottom) before and after
recapture, and how many months they were lapsed. The analysis also includes supporting information-such as the donor s
most recent gift year and their giving status in the latest fully closed fiscal year-which, while not core to the recapture
calculation, can help you craft more personalized outreach and stewardship plans. For instance, you can readily spot if a
recaptured donor has since lapsed again, or if their giving level has increased, decreased, or stayed steady since
reactivation. Key metrics calculated include the months lapsed between gifts, the giving levels before and after recapture
(based on your organization's thresholds), and the timing of the most recent gifts. These insights matter because they reveal
not just who you have recaptured, but how donor behavior changes across their lifecycle, helping you refine strategies for
lapsed donor campaigns, stewardship, and upgrade efforts. You should have your constituent engagement, annual giving,
and stewardship teams review this analysis regularly-ideally as part of your Constituent Intelligence routines. Use the
findings to prioritize outreach to recently recaptured donors, especially those whose giving levels dropped or who may be at
risk of lapsing again. Consider tailoring stewardship efforts to acknowledge their return and reinforce their renewed
relationship with your organization. Development officers can leverage the lapsed and recapture history to personalize
communications, focusing on donors who demonstrated resilience or upward giving trends after being recaptured. Measure
success by tracking retention among recaptured donors, increases in their giving levels post-recapture, and a reduction in
the length of lapsed periods over time. Ultimately, this analysis empowers you to make more informed decisions about
donor engagement, helping you increase lifetime value and strengthen donor loyalty.

All Donor Recaptures (10yr) - All recapture events How to use the All Donor Recaptures (10yr) - All recapture events

giving levels changed before and after recapture. This analytic identifies all recapture events.  Over a ten-year analysis

not have been properly stewarded to ensure annual giving consistency.  The analysis incorporates both individual and
organizational donors, automatically pulling the appropriate name and tracking their giving across fiscal years using your
organization's segmentation tiers (Top, Middle, Bottom), so you can quickly see at what giving level the donor was before

follow-up tasks to portfolio managers for donors who exhibit multiple recaptures or have returned at higher giving levels. Use
the months lapsed metric to test new timing for reactivation campaigns, and leverage giving level changes to craft
personalized messaging that recognizes renewed commitment. Measure the success of this analysis by tracking increases
in recapture rates, upgrades in giving following targeted outreach, and improvements in the speed at which lapsed donors
return. Ultimately, integrating these insights into your strategy will help you build stronger, more resilient donor relationships
and optimize your fundraising outcomes.

 QX98   Donor Tier Upgrade Pathways Summary Analysis
What are the data-driven gift size benchmarks (25th, 50th, 75th percentile) for our Top, Middle, and Bottom donor
segments, and the number of donors each.
Donor Tier Upgrade Pathways Summary How to use the Donor Tier Upgrade Pathways Summary analysis This analysis
gives you a high-level view of where your donors stand within your current giving tiers, typically labeled as Top, Middle, and
Bottom, based on their total giving in the most recent full fiscal year. By analyzing all gifts from donors during that time, it
segments donors according to thresholds you've set, then examines the size and frequency of their individual gifts. The
central insight you gain is the identification of donors in lower tiers who are already making gifts comparable to those in
higher segments, highlighting strong upgrade opportunities. The core of the analysis calculates key percentile benchmarks
for each donor segment: the 25th, 50th (median), and 75th percentile gift amounts. It then identifies how many donors in
each segment are making gifts at or above the median and top quartile for their tier. This allows you to spot Middle and
Bottom tier donors whose giving behavior resembles that of higher-level supporters. You can also view the total number of
gifts per segment, which helps you gauge engagement and identify trends in donor behavior. You can use this analysis to
prioritize outreach and stewardship. For example, if you notice a significant group of Middle segment donors making gifts
above the 75th percentile for their tier, consider targeting them for personalized upgrade campaigns or enhanced
recognition.  Development directors, annual giving managers, and major gift officers should review this analysis as part of
regular Constituent Intelligence routines-ideally after each fiscal quarter or fundraising campaign. Use the insights to select
upgrade candidates and tailor your touchpoints. For actionable steps: assign staff to connect with donors flagged in the
upper percentile ranges, test targeted upgrade asks, and monitor their response to personalized engagement. To measure
success, track the rate of donor upgrades by segment, the lift in total giving among prioritized donors, and retention rates of
those who received targeted outreach. Over time, you should see increases in the number of donors moving into higher
segments, along with improved donor loyalty and lifetime value.
